text:
I've made this recipe several times since my initial review two years ago.  As I was printing off the recipe for this Christmas prep, I read some of the more recent comments, and decided to add what I've learned in the past couple years: there's a big difference between doing it the day before vs the same day.  When made the day before, it's stiffer and the sour cream and garlic (if you add that, as I do) are twice as strong.  Much too strong, in my opinion.  And you will need to re-mash with milk and butter to fluff it up, which means you lose half the benefit of doing it ahead of time.

I HIGHLY recommend doing it only a few hours before (3 or 4 has been just right, for me) and then putting it in a slow cooker on low until dinner.  The flavor is prefect and it's still fluffy.

text:
This recipe was a huge hit at my potluck party! Everyone complimented on the dish, moreso than the entree (that person wasn't too thrilled that I one up-ed him). I used suggestions from others' reviews. Here's my variation on the recipe: I used yukon gold potatoes, onion & chives cream cheese, and garlic salt instead on onion salt. Followed recipe as stated, but prior to baking I used 1/2 cup of whipping cream and butter to moisten the potatoes. Mixed in some bacon bits and cheddard cheese. Topped off with bacon bits and cheddar cheese before baking. The end result...my dish was completely empty and still had people begging for more.

text:
This has been my 'signature' recipe for our mashed potatoes since Thanksgiving 2002!!  I always get raves about them.  My husband won't let me make our mashed potatoes any other way, because he says, 'nothing compares'!  The 'signature' really boils down to the cream cheese, because many mashed potato recipes are made with the other ingredients, but the cream cheese really sets these apart from all others!  However, I do make it slightly different from what the recipe calls for.  I also add a little skim milk to it, as well as use fat-free cream cheese and sour cream, and interchange using onion powder one time and garlic powder the next, just for variety.  And, of course, the measurements of the ingredients are never the same each time, so I put a little in of everything until it's just right, smooth and creamy.  I've never made these potatoes the 'day before', but serve right away.  However, I always make enough for leftovers and they're delicious cold or hot the next day!  Give these a try, you won't be disappointed!  :)  Thank you so much, Erin, for the wonderful recipe!

I know this recipe as twice baked potatoes...and it is WONDERFUL!!!  I have made these potatoes for years and my family always demands it at all occasions.  I do a few things different though.  Instead of baking next day...I put the potatoes into a crock pot and slice a 1/4 stick butter onto the top and refrigerate until Thanksgiving morning...cover and cook on high till heated threw.  Saves on oven space.  I also mix in (to taste) fresh green onions...adds color to the dish and a wonderful taste!

text:
Excellent...and you don't need to make the day before!  Those of you who said your potatoes weren't creamy probably used big bakers.  I agree that the recipe should specify what kind of potato or the approximate poundage.  I used  9  red potatoes (about 2 lbs.)and the recipe came out very creamy.  Red potatoes have a wonderful texture and mash very easily. They're also about half the size of an  Idaho.  Don't  bother peeling the potatoes--it's unnecessary labor, and the skins provide color and nutrients.   I  increased the amount of salt and pepper a bit, and only used 3 oz. of cream cheese.  Otherwise,  excellent.  My very southern husband loved them.

text:
This recipe has incredible possibilities. It is lacking only MILK. I added enough to make the potatoes very light and fluffy, while beating in my KitchenAid. Out of personal preference I now use about double the sour cream, more or less, and NO CREAM CHEESE (I did not like the twice-baked potato taste it gave. I want a mashed-potato taste). Used half white pepper, half black. More butter. Finally, remove from refrigerator at least an hour before baking. Bake 40 min covered, and 20 minutes uncovered. A light sprinkling of white cheddar or Parmesan (or Trader Joe's shredded Quattro Formaggio- YUM!), a bit of melted butter, and paprika ended in a restaurant-quality dish! 2/15/12

I have gotten requests to make this for holiday dinners and cookouts. Use the Yukon Golds, they blend up very creamy!  Add a couple tsp. garlic powder or some chopped garlic too! After experimenting, I now always use neufchatel (low-fat) cream cheese and reduced-fat sour cream. You honestly can't tell a difference. text:
These potatoes were great. I doubled the recipe (2) 5 lb bags and followed it exactly. I didn't have a potatoe ricer so I used my hand mixer. I boiled the potatoes (cubed) in a huge pot, until they were soft. I drained them, put them back in the pot and slowly added the rest of the ingredients. I whipped everything together and then put the pot in the refrigerator. The next day I transferred them to a 13x9 pan, stuck a few pats of butter in the potatoes and heated it for about 1/2 hour. The top will get a light golden brown if you do not cover it. They were so fluffy and moist. The flavor was great.

text:
I made these for Thanksgiving dinner, and they were really great. I made them same-day as others had suggested, and let them heat in the crockpot on 'warm' until dinner. I think that is the way to go,as they were already drying out by the time we packed up the leftovers, but still great reheated the next day. I did make a few changes. I added extra cream cheese, 1/4 cup milk and 1/4 cup of water from the pot they were boiled in (I read about that in another recipe)during the mashing process. I mashed them in the crockpot, thinking I was saving myself time (I ended up making a big mess, I wouldn't do it that way again). I also added butter on top while they warmed, and stirred it all in at the last minute before serving. I also skipped the onion powder because one reviewer stated that they tasted like sour cream and onion chips, and that didn't seem appropriate for thanksgiving dinner. I will definitely make these again, next time I will make the recipe as is, just not for a big dinner until I know what it tastes like. I will also continue to tweak them for my family's taste, but all in all, a really good recipe and I'm glad that I tried it for my first attempt at Thanksgiving mashed potatoes!

text:
This recipe is EXCELLENT, absolutely THE BEST.  Family and friends beg me to make these potatoes all the time. They are delicious served the day of and even better the day after. I have found that if the taste of sour cream is to overpowering, use plain yogurt. To make them creamy and fluffy use an electric hand mixer after mashing with masher. Don't over mix or they'll get pasty and sticky. To cut the fat use nonfat plain yogurt, fat free cream cheese, lite salt and lowfat butter spread or margarine.Whoever doesn't love this recipe is either crazy or doing something wrong.

Baked it for 30 minutes, and these were some great spuds! Next time, I'll try adding some cheddar!Thanks so much for this recipe!!

I use a version similar to this that I've used for 15 years, originally from my step-mother's Junior League cookbook.  I make it well in advance (several days) and freeze it. Absolutely great idea. And simple as potatoes. Few tips. Sour cream and cream cheese can be fat free or Lite or with chive and/or onion flavor.
Skim milk poured over top will absorb into mash. I do this before I refrigerate and also before baking to loosen it up. And I also put some cheese on top before baking, then after baking I stir. While cooking I season to taste. Maybe a little more onion powder. Sometimes I add a LITTLE garlic salt for a LITTLE kick. Feel free to contact me. I make this at least once a month.

text:
I gambled and made this the night before Thanksgiving.  The night before they were moist, and smelled great.  All right, I did steal a little taste and they were wonderful!  However, after sitting overnight and cooking in the oven on Thanksgiving Day they became totally dried out and stiff.  An embarrassment.  It would not have been a time saver to "tweak" these taters at the last minute, either.  It would have just been safer to peel the potatoes ahead of time and make them at the last minute as usual.  And a lot less fattening, too, to do it the old-fashioned way, I might add.

text:
What a great recipe. I made these mashed potatoes the night before Thanksgiving. I stored them in my crockpot inside of my refrigerator overnight. In the morning, when I put in my turkey, I put on the crockpot od potatoes. They warmed through the morning and were moist and ready to eat in perfect time with the turkey. What an easy way to prepare ahead of time and they tasted as if they were made that morning. In fact, most of the potatoes were gone before our Thanksgiving meal from guest sampling the potatoes all morning as they were warming. They all loved the taste. I followed the recipe as stated and added a little butter to moisten as they warmed throughout the morning. They didn't really need to be moistened however...I just love butter. I WILL make these again and save myself the hassle while preparing a meal.

Pretty good recipe...I thought the onion flavor was a little strong at first but after they set overnight in the fridge, it blended nicely.  I let the mixture set at room temperature for thirty minutes prior to baking them.  I baked for 30 minutes like the recipe states and the potatoes were still cold.  I stirred, kept in for ten more minutes and it wasn't doing the trick.  I wound up having to finish them in the microwave.  I added some additional pats of butter to make the potatoes less clumpy and stirred in some milk prior to serving to make the potatoes creamier.  Definitely a time saver being able to prepare ahead of time...now I know to either plan for a longer baking time or I will just use the microwave.  I may give the slow cooker a try sometime and see how they turn out using that...this recipe is a keeper though, slight modifications could be made to suit anyone's tastes.

These were very rich and tasty, but had some small lumps. I cooked until still slightly firm but enough to break apart easily when forked thinking they would continue to cook some the next day & didn't want mushy or gluey potatoes. I refrigerated in a glass container overnight then transferred to a non-stick sprayed crockpot to heat for about 2.5 hours on low (then put on 'warm' while serving) to save room in the oven. Worked great & had lots of compliments!

I had made the potatoes the night before & refrigerated overnight. So if you do them the day before please allow 3 hrs on high to get them warmed up again.

I used 5 lbs yukon gold, 1/4 cup each shredded swiss & monterey jack cheese, green onions and crumbled bacon! put butter pats down into the mixture and stored in butter coated crock pot for 3 days prior. On Low, they were ready in about 2 hours, so I had to lower to Warm. Stired a few times for a few more hours, and added some milk to the mixture to keep it from drying out. This is an awesome recipe and I will make many more times! Guests loved it, but for 8 people, I should have made more (like a 5# bag plus half of another bag). text:
I first made this several years ago, and since then, I am EXPECTED to bring it to every family Thanksgiving and Christmas dinner. :)
I use 5 lbs of russets, and the whole 8 oz brick of cream cheese, since that's how it comes from the store. 

Make sure your boiled potatoes are DRY after draining the water,  before mixing in the other ingredients, and that the cream cheese and butter are very soft. Those steps are KEY.

text:
I was surprised at how much I liked these because I'm not the biggest fan of cream cheese.  Being able to make it ahead of time was so useful for Thanksgiving dinner.

UPDATE:  I've made these a few times since then and the one thing I've learned is to throw the potatoes after cubing, cover with water, then heat to boiling and boil for 15 minutes from the point it starts boiling.  The potatoes are much easier to mash since they've been in the hot water a little bit longer.

As for the texture, these are heavier than most mashed potatoes, which is something that I prefer.

text:
These potatoes are Killer!!  I made them the day before & you do not have to worry that they wonât be delish the next day. For Thanksgiving, I opted to not add any cheese to the casserole, though I certainly will for other meals.
I used 10 MED/LG  Russet potatoes, 8 oz. cream cheese, whole milk, and easily 4T of Plugra butter. salt & pepper to taste.   I added 6 cloves of peeled, fresh garlic cloves to the boiling potato water. Do not overlook these boiled potatoes as they will become elastic.    
I drained, mashed (potatoes & garlic),  then added other ingredients, placed all in an 8x8 greased casserole dish (you can use 9x9 or 9x13 ):  let cool COMPLETELY.   I pricked several holes in the top, filled those w a little milk, dabbed on even more butter, covered & refrigerated. Thanksgiving morning I took them out, uncovered, & let come to room temperature.  About 2 1/2 hours before dinner time, I put the potatoes into my crock pot on LOW.  3 hrs is the max or they will get brown at edges of pot. I did add a bit of warmed milk, more butter & salt while they were warming.
You will be HAPPY.  These are delicious & itâs nice to be able to prepare these ahead & not need to tie up oven space.
Enjoy!

text:
There are many reasons why this recipe works.  For one, you can totally make this healthy.  Go for fat free sour cream and cream cheese and it's got so little butter that it doesn't matter.  For the basic mashed potatoes its usually a stick of butter and  heavy cream or the boxed stuff that tastes like cardboard with herbs and have more salt than the Pacific ocean...no ty!  Two, we loved the taste of this one.  Not bland, and the cream cheese was a neat twist.  I used a mixer to make it extra creamy (personal preference), added onion flakes instead of powder and pretty much added amounts to taste.  I also ate this same day, so no oven (nothing to cook anyway).  Last, I paired this up with Glazed Meatloaf II...what a meal!  Definitely recommend this one.

text:
I've made these many times and they're ALWAYS a crowd pleaser. Since my time is usually short (two toddlers 18 months apart), I don't even peel the potatoes. Also, I don't bake these. I just serve them right after I mush everything together (in the crock pot). That way they are still moist (and saves time). They taste great reheated with cheese and bacon on top.  Oh, By the way...if any of you are new to cooking, DON"T try to "mash" these in a food processor!!! They end up being a gluey mess. I learned this the hard way as I was trying to cook an impressive meal for my in-laws when I was first married. They certainly made an impression! Just not the one I was going for! :)

text:
I made these for Thanksgiving early in the day so I wouldn't take up the stove. I followed review's suggestions, and used chive cream cheese and added extra garlic powder and onion powder, and fried a couple of garlic cloves chopped before I mashed the potatoes. They still weren't too garlicy. I kept them warm in the crock pot, they stayed soft and creamy until dinner, and they were a real hit with the crowd! The leftovers warmed up MUCH better than normal mashed potatoes! They are richer than I would make on a regular basis, but they were great for a special occasion.

text:
These potatoes were VERY good when we first made them.  However, after refrigerating overnight, as many other reviewers have posted, they get very dry and hard and dense.  Before cooking the next day I mixed in some milk and that helped a little, but you lose that freshly made texture by refrigerating for several hours.   Overall they had a nice flavor, but I would recommend getting all the ingredients together and making these right before serving.  I would give that recipe 5 stars.   The texture and consistency just gets lost and that's why I can only give this 3 stars.  No rave reviews from the Thanksgiving guests on this one.

text:
This recipe really helped me out on Thanksgiving day when I have so much to do. I actually did this in the morning while the turkey was in the oven. So, I made these and just dumped them into the crock pot hot. If I had chilled them overnight, I would have used others suggestion to poke holes in the potatoes with a fork and then pour milk and butter over the top so they don't dry out. I would also stir every hour. Then I would put on low for at least 2.5 hours before dinner. I boiled 4 garlic cloves with my 8 lbs of potatoes for some flavoring. I have also used chive flavored cream cheese... Sometimes I also use shredded cheddar cheese and crumbled bacon bits for a baked potato resemblance. Or you can top with shredded mozzarella cheese. PS Don't forget to spray the crock pot with pam before adding potatoes, so they don't stick.

text:
I just made this dish for Thanksgiving today (11/27/03, and they came out really good.  I made one mistake - I over mixed them, and as we all know, when you over whip potatoes, they get glutinous.  So, to fix the problem, I took another recipe from Allrecipe.com and combined it with this one.  I beat a couple of eggs into the potatoe mixture, snipped a few fresh chives, and baked it at 350 degrees for about 1/2 hour.  They were the fluffiest most wonderful tasting potatoes we have ever had.  Everone was very impressed with them.  Even if I hadn't over-whipped the potatoes, the eggs would have made them better anyway!  I'm telling you - it sounds a little funky, but try it, it is worth it!
